<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Gwyneth Paltrow</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">

<p><b>Gwyneth Kate Paltrow</b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'g' in 'guy'">ɡ</span><span title="'w' in 'wind'">w</span><span title="/ɪ/ short 'i' in 'bid'">ɪ</span><span title="'n' in 'no'">n</span><span title="/ɪ/ or /ə/ 'e' in 'roses'">ᵻ</span><span title="/θ/ 'th' in 'thigh'">θ</span></span> <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="/æ/ short 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/oʊ/ long 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span></span>/</a></span></span>; born September 27, 1972)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> is an American actress, singer, and food writer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> She gained early notice for her work in films such as the thriller <i><a href="/wiki/Seven_(1995_film)" title="Seven (1995 film)">Seven</a></i> (1995) and the period drama <i><a href="/wiki/Emma_(1996_theatrical_film)" title="Emma (1996 theatrical film)">Emma</a></i> (1996). Following starring roles in the romantic comedy-drama <i><a href="/wiki/Sliding_Doors" title="Sliding Doors">Sliding Doors</a></i> (1998) and the thriller <i><a href="/wiki/A_Perfect_Murder" title="A Perfect Murder">A Perfect Murder</a></i> (1998), Paltrow garnered worldwide recognition through her performance in <i><a href="/wiki/Shakespeare_in_Love" title="Shakespeare in Love">Shakespeare in Love</a></i> (1998), for which she won an <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Actress" title="Academy Award for Best Actress">Academy Award</a>, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Actress_%E2%80%93_Motion_Picture_Musical_or_Comedy" title="Golden Globe Award for Best Actress – Motion Picture Musical or Comedy">Golden Globe Award</a> and two <a href="/wiki/Screen_Actors_Guild_Award_for_Outstanding_Performance_by_a_Female_Actor_in_a_Leading_Role" title="Screen Actors Guild Award for Outstanding Performance by a Female Actor in a Leading Role">Screen Actors Guild Awards</a>. Paltrow has portrayed supporting, as well as lead roles, in films such as <i><a href="/wiki/The_Talented_Mr._Ripley_(film)" title="The Talented Mr. Ripley (film)">The Talented Mr. Ripley</a></i> (1999), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Royal_Tenenbaums" title="The Royal Tenenbaums">The Royal Tenenbaums</a></i> (2001), <i><a href="/wiki/Shallow_Hal" title="Shallow Hal">Shallow Hal</a></i> (2001), and <i><a href="/wiki/Proof_(2005_film)" title="Proof (2005 film)">Proof</a></i> (2005), for which she earned a <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Actress_in_a_Motion_Picture_%E2%80%93_Drama" title="Golden Globe Award for Best Actress in a Motion Picture – Drama">Golden Globe</a> nomination.</p>
<p>Since 2008, Paltrow has portrayed <a href="/wiki/Pepper_Potts" title="Pepper Potts">Pepper Potts</a>, the female lead of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iron_Man_(film_series)" title="Iron Man (film series)">Iron Man franchise</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe" title="Marvel Cinematic Universe">Marvel Cinematic Universe</a>, in <i><a href="/wiki/Iron_Man_(2008_film)" title="Iron Man (2008 film)">Iron Man</a></i> (2008), <i><a href="/wiki/Iron_Man_2" title="Iron Man 2">Iron Man 2</a></i> (2010), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Avengers_(2012_film)" title="The Avengers (2012 film)">The Avengers</a></i> (2012), and <i><a href="/wiki/Iron_Man_3" title="Iron Man 3">Iron Man 3</a></i> (2013). She won a <a href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Award" title="Primetime Emmy Award">Primetime Emmy Award</a> for <a href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Award_for_Outstanding_Guest_Actress_in_a_Comedy_Series" title="Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Guest Actress in a Comedy Series">Outstanding Guest Actress in a Comedy Series</a> in 2011 for her role as <a href="/wiki/Holly_Holliday" title="Holly Holliday">Holly Holliday</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company" title="Fox Broadcasting Company">Fox</a> television series <i><a href="/wiki/Glee_(TV_series)" title="Glee (TV series)">Glee</a></i>, her first and so far only foray into television acting. She reprised the role several other times throughout the series' run.</p>
<p>Following relationships with <a href="/wiki/Brad_Pitt" title="Brad Pitt">Brad Pitt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ben_Affleck" title="Ben Affleck">Ben Affleck</a>, Paltrow married <a href="/wiki/Chris_Martin" title="Chris Martin">Chris Martin</a>, the lead vocalist of band <a href="/wiki/Coldplay" title="Coldplay">Coldplay</a>, in 2003; they have two children. They announced their separation in March 2014 and divorced in July 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-people.com_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-people.com-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> Paltrow has been dating television executive <a href="/wiki/Brad_Falchuk" title="Brad Falchuk">Brad Falchuk</a> since August 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usmagazine.com_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-usmagazine.com-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>Paltrow has been the face of <a href="/wiki/Est%C3%A9e_Lauder_Companies" title="Estée Lauder Companies">Estée Lauder</a>'s Pleasures perfume since 2005. She is also the face of American fashion brand <a href="/wiki/Coach,_Inc." title="Coach, Inc.">Coach</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> owner of a lifestyle company, and author of two cookbooks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life_and_education">Early life and education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwyneth_Paltrow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life and education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Paltrow was born in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>, the daughter of actress <a href="/wiki/Blythe_Danner" title="Blythe Danner">Blythe Danner</a> and film producer/director <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Paltrow" title="Bruce Paltrow">Bruce Paltrow</a>. Paltrow's father is <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jewish</a>, while her mother is from a <a href="/wiki/Christian" title="Christian">Christian</a> background. She was raised celebrating "both Jewish and Christian holidays."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> Her brother had a traditional <a href="/wiki/Bar_and_Bat_Mitzvah" title="Bar and Bat Mitzvah">Bar Mitzvah</a> when he turned 13.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>Her father's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ashkenazi_Jewish" title="Ashkenazi Jewish">Ashkenazi Jewish</a> family immigrated from <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> and Poland,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brown_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-brown-16">[16]</a></sup> while her mother has <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Dutch" title="Pennsylvania Dutch">Pennsylvania Dutch</a> (German), and some <a href="/wiki/White_Barbadian" title="White Barbadian">white Barbadian</a> (English), ancestry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> Paltrow's paternal great-great-grandfather, was a <a href="/wiki/Rabbi" title="Rabbi">rabbi</a> in <a href="/wiki/Nowogr%C3%B3d" title="Nowogród">Nowogród</a>, Poland, and a descendant of the well known "Paltrowicz" family of rabbis from <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w" title="Kraków">Kraków</a>, whose best known descendant is R. <a href="/wiki/David_HaLevi_Segal" title="David HaLevi Segal">David HaLevi Segal</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Paltrow's younger brother is director and screenwriter <a href="/wiki/Jake_Paltrow" title="Jake Paltrow">Jake Paltrow</a>. Her half-cousin is actress <a href="/wiki/Katherine_Moennig" title="Katherine Moennig">Katherine Moennig</a> (through her mother). She is a second cousin of former U.S. Congresswoman <a href="/wiki/Gabrielle_Giffords" title="Gabrielle Giffords">Gabrielle Giffords</a> (<a href="/wiki/Arizona%27s_8th_congressional_district" title="Arizona's 8th congressional district">AZ-08</a>) (through her father).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atyliao_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-atyliao-22">[22]</a></sup> Her uncle is opera singer and actor <a href="/wiki/Harry_Danner" title="Harry Danner">Harry Danner</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Paltrow was raised in <a href="/wiki/Santa_Monica,_California" title="Santa Monica, California">Santa Monica</a>, where she attended <a href="/wiki/Crossroads_School_(Santa_Monica,_California)" title="Crossroads School (Santa Monica, California)">Crossroads School</a> before enrolling in the <a href="/wiki/Spence_School" title="Spence School">Spence School</a>, a private girls' school in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EW_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-EW-23">[23]</a></sup> Later, she briefly studied anthropology at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Santa_Barbara" title="University of California, Santa Barbara">University of California, Santa Barbara</a>, before dropping out to act.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MyPlan_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-MyPlan-24">[24]</a></sup> She is an "adopted daughter" of <a href="/wiki/Talavera_de_la_Reina" title="Talavera de la Reina">Talavera de la Reina</a> (Spain), where at 15 she spent a year as an <a href="/wiki/Student_exchange_program" title="Student exchange program">exchange student</a> and learned to speak Spanish.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-heart_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-heart-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwyneth_Paltrow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1989.E2.80.9395:_Early_acting_work">1989–95: Early acting work</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwyneth_Paltrow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1989–95: Early acting work">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Her acting debut was in <i>High</i> (1989), a TV film her father directed, and after spending several summers watching her mother perform at the <a href="/wiki/Williamstown_Theatre_Festival" title="Williamstown Theatre Festival">Williamstown Theatre Festival</a> in <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">Massachusetts</a>, Paltrow made her professional stage debut there in 1990.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yahoo_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo-28">[28]</a></sup> Her film debut followed with <i><a href="/wiki/Shout_(film)" title="Shout (film)">Shout</a></i> (1991), starring <a href="/wiki/John_Travolta" title="John Travolta">John Travolta</a>; and she was cast by <a href="/wiki/Steven_Spielberg" title="Steven Spielberg">Steven Spielberg</a> in his film <i><a href="/wiki/Hook_(film)" title="Hook (film)">Hook</a></i> (1991) as the young <a href="/wiki/Wendy_Darling" title="Wendy Darling">Wendy Darling</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yahoo_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>Paltrow's next roles were in the made-for-television movies <i><a href="/wiki/Cruel_Doubt" title="Cruel Doubt">Cruel Doubt</a></i> (1992) and <i><a href="/wiki/Deadly_Relations" title="Deadly Relations">Deadly Relations</a></i> (1993). Her first plum feature film role was in the noir drama <i><a href="/wiki/Flesh_and_Bone_(film)" title="Flesh and Bone (film)">Flesh and Bone</a></i> (1993) as the much-younger girlfriend of <a href="/wiki/James_Caan" title="James Caan">James Caan</a>. In 1995, she played <a href="/wiki/Brad_Pitt" title="Brad Pitt">Brad Pitt</a>'s wife in the hit thriller <i><a href="/wiki/Seven_(1995_film)" title="Seven (1995 film)">Se7en</a></i>. Her performance earned her a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Satellite_Award" title="Satellite Award">Satellite Award</a> nomination. Also in 1995, she appeared in <i><a href="/wiki/Moonlight_and_Valentino" title="Moonlight and Valentino">Moonlight and Valentino</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Jefferson_in_Paris" title="Jefferson in Paris">Jefferson in Paris</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1996.E2.80.932001:_Breakthrough_and_film_stardom">1996–2001: Breakthrough and film stardom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwyneth_Paltrow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1996–2001: Breakthrough and film stardom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1996, Paltrow played the title character in <i><a href="/wiki/Emma_(1996_theatrical_film)" title="Emma (1996 theatrical film)">Emma</a></i> to critical acclaim, particularly in the United Kingdom, where her perfection of the English accent was appreciated. She had leading roles in several films throughout 1998, including <i><a href="/wiki/Sliding_Doors" title="Sliding Doors">Sliding Doors</a></i> and the adaptation of the <a href="/wiki/Charles_Dickens" title="Charles Dickens">Charles Dickens</a> novel <i><a href="/wiki/Great_Expectations_(1998_film)" title="Great Expectations (1998 film)">Great Expectations</a></i> with <a href="/wiki/Ethan_Hawke" title="Ethan Hawke">Ethan Hawke</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_De_Niro" title="Robert De Niro">Robert De Niro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anne_Bancroft" title="Anne Bancroft">Anne Bancroft</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chris_Cooper" title="Chris Cooper">Chris Cooper</a>. She also appeared in two thrillers, <i><a href="/wiki/Hush_(1998_film)" title="Hush (1998 film)">Hush</a></i>, opposite <a href="/wiki/Jessica_Lange" title="Jessica Lange">Jessica Lange</a>, and <i><a href="/wiki/A_Perfect_Murder" title="A Perfect Murder">A Perfect Murder</a></i>, inspired by <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Hitchcock" title="Alfred Hitchcock">Alfred Hitchcock</a>'s 1954 film, <i><a href="/wiki/Dial_M_for_Murder" title="Dial M for Murder">Dial M for Murder</a></i>. In the latter film, Paltrow starred opposite <a href="/wiki/Michael_Douglas" title="Michael Douglas">Michael Douglas</a>, playing Emily Taylor, who was based on <a href="/wiki/Grace_Kelly" title="Grace Kelly">Grace Kelly</a>'s character from the original film, though the film was met with mixed reviews. She was also considered for the role of Rose DeWitt Bukater in the 1997 film <i><a href="/wiki/Titanic_(1997_film)" title="Titanic (1997 film)">Titanic</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GwynethPaltrowTIFF00_adj.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1078" data-file-width="682" height="348" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/GwynethPaltrowTIFF00_adj.jpg/220px-GwynethPaltrowTIFF00_adj.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/GwynethPaltrowTIFF00_adj.jpg/330px-GwynethPaltrowTIFF00_adj.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/GwynethPaltrowTIFF00_adj.jpg/440px-GwynethPaltrowTIFF00_adj.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GwynethPaltrowTIFF00_adj.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Paltrow at the 2000 <a href="/wiki/Toronto_International_Film_Festival" title="Toronto International Film Festival">Toronto International Film Festival</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1998, Paltrow starred in <i><a href="/wiki/Shakespeare_in_Love" title="Shakespeare in Love">Shakespeare in Love</a></i>, portraying the fictional lover of <a href="/wiki/William_Shakespeare" title="William Shakespeare">William Shakespeare</a>, played by <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Fiennes" title="Joseph Fiennes">Joseph Fiennes</a>. The film earned US$289 million in box office receipts, and Paltrow gained critical acclaim for her portrayal. <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i> commented, "Best of all is Gwyneth Paltrow, who, at long last, has a movie to star in that's as radiant as she is."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> summed up her performance as Viola thus: "Gwyneth Paltrow, in her first great, fully realized starring performance, makes a heroine so breathtaking that she seems utterly plausible as the playwright's guiding light."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>The award-winning <i>Shakespeare in Love</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nyt-oscars99_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-oscars99-35">[35]</a></sup> earned Paltrow the award for Outstanding Performance by a Female Actor in a Leading Role from the <a href="/wiki/Screen_Actors_Guild" title="Screen Actors Guild">Screen Actors Guild</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shakespeare_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-Shakespeare-36">[36]</a></sup> the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Actress_-_Motion_Picture_Musical_or_Comedy" title="Golden Globe Award for Best Actress - Motion Picture Musical or Comedy">Golden Globe Award for Best Actress</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shakespeare_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-Shakespeare-36">[36]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Actress" title="Academy Award for Best Actress">Academy Award for Best Actress</a>, among other honors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nyt-oscars99_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-oscars99-35">[35]</a></sup> Her <a href="/wiki/Pink_Ralph_Lauren_dress_of_Gwyneth_Paltrow" title="Pink Ralph Lauren dress of Gwyneth Paltrow">Pink Ralph Lauren dress</a> worn at the <a href="/wiki/71st_Academy_Awards" title="71st Academy Awards">71st Academy Awards</a> in collecting her Oscar was extremely popular and was credited for bringing pink back into fashion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GaleKaur2004_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-GaleKaur2004-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1999, Paltrow co-starred alongside <a href="/wiki/Jude_Law" title="Jude Law">Jude Law</a>, <a href="/wiki/Matt_Damon" title="Matt Damon">Matt Damon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cate_Blanchett" title="Cate Blanchett">Cate Blanchett</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Talented_Mr._Ripley_(film)" title="The Talented Mr. Ripley (film)">The Talented Mr. Ripley</a></i>, which earned $80 million domestically and received positive reviews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> She showcased her singing ability in 2000's <i><a href="/wiki/Duets_(film)" title="Duets (film)">Duets</a></i>, which was directed by her father and co-starred singer <a href="/wiki/Huey_Lewis" title="Huey Lewis">Huey Lewis</a>. The same year, Paltrow co-starred with <a href="/wiki/Ben_Affleck" title="Ben Affleck">Ben Affleck</a> in the romantic drama <i><a href="/wiki/Bounce_(film)" title="Bounce (film)">Bounce</a></i> as Abby Janello. In 2001, she played Margot Tenenbaum as part of an ensemble cast in the <a href="/wiki/Wes_Anderson" title="Wes Anderson">Wes Anderson</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Royal_Tenenbaums" title="The Royal Tenenbaums">The Royal Tenenbaums</a></i> and starred with <a href="/wiki/Jack_Black" title="Jack Black">Jack Black</a> in the comedy <i><a href="/wiki/Shallow_Hal" title="Shallow Hal">Shallow Hal</a></i>, where she had to wear a specially designed 25-pound fatsuit and heavy make-up.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2002.E2.80.9307:_Career_slowdown_and_hiatus">2002–07: Career slowdown and hiatus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwyneth_Paltrow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2002–07: Career slowdown and hiatus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since the Oscar for <i>Shakespeare in Love</i>, Paltrow's film career has been less noteworthy and critical acclaim has waned.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> She said she was unequipped for the pressure, leading to several bad movie choices,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> agreeing with peers who believe the win is, in some ways, a curse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> During this time, Paltrow rarely appeared in films, having taken a hiatus to raise her two children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EW_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-EW-23">[23]</a></sup> In <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i>, she said she divided her career into movies for love and films for money: <i>The Royal Tenenbaums</i>, <i>Proof</i>, and <i>Sylvia</i> fell into the former category, while she signed on to <i><a href="/wiki/View_from_the_Top" title="View from the Top">View from the Top</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Shallow_Hal" title="Shallow Hal">Shallow Hal</a></i> for the latter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-heart_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-heart-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2004, she starred in the science-fiction film <i><a href="/wiki/Sky_Captain_and_the_World_of_Tomorrow" title="Sky Captain and the World of Tomorrow">Sky Captain and the World of Tomorrow</a></i> opposite Jude Law. The same year, she was recognized as an outstanding woman in entertainment by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Women_in_Film_Los_Angeles" title="Women in Film Los Angeles">Women in Film Los Angeles</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Women_in_Film_Crystal_%2B_Lucy_Awards#THE_CRYSTAL_AWARD" title="Women in Film Crystal + Lucy Awards">Crystal Award</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> In 2005, she starred in the film <i><a href="/wiki/Proof_(2005_film)" title="Proof (2005 film)">Proof</a></i> as the depressed daughter of a brilliant, eccentric mathematician. The movie was based on the <a href="/wiki/Proof_(play)" title="Proof (play)">play of the same name</a>, in which Paltrow also played the same character at London's <a href="/wiki/Donmar_Warehouse" title="Donmar Warehouse">Donmar Warehouse</a> in 2002. For her film performance, Paltrow earned her second Golden Globe nomination for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Actress_%E2%80%93_Motion_Picture_Drama" title="Golden Globe Award for Best Actress – Motion Picture Drama">Best Actress – Motion Picture Drama</a>. In 2006, she had small roles in <i><a href="/wiki/Running_with_Scissors_(film)" title="Running with Scissors (film)">Running With Scissors</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Infamous_(film)" title="Infamous (film)">Infamous</a></i>, in which she sang <a href="/wiki/Cole_Porter" title="Cole Porter">Cole Porter</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/What_Is_This_Thing_Called_Love%3F" title="What Is This Thing Called Love?">What Is This Thing Called Love?</a>".</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2008.E2.80.93present:_Iron_Man_and_career_rejuvenation">2008–present: <i>Iron Man</i> and career rejuvenation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwyneth_Paltrow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2008–present: Iron Man and career rejuvenation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2008, she appeared in the superhero film <i><a href="/wiki/Iron_Man_(2008_film)" title="Iron Man (2008 film)">Iron Man</a></i> as <a href="/wiki/Pepper_Potts" title="Pepper Potts">Pepper Potts</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tony_Stark" title="Tony Stark">Tony Stark</a>'s personal assistant, closest friend, and budding love interest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> <i>Iron Man</i> was Paltrow's highest-grossing film to date, earning more than $585,000,000 worldwide,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> until she reprised her role as Potts in <a href="/wiki/Joss_Whedon" title="Joss Whedon">Joss Whedon</a>'s 2012 superhero film, <a href="/wiki/The_Avengers_(2012_film)" title="The Avengers (2012 film)">The Avengers</a>, which grossed more than $1 billion worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> Paltrow said she was hesitant to appear in a big-budget project but she was won over by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Robert_Downey,_Jr." title="Robert Downey, Jr.">Robert Downey, Jr.</a>, the film's lead, and director <a href="/wiki/Jon_Favreau" title="Jon Favreau">Jon Favreau</a>. She recalled a conversation with Downey, saying:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Catherine_Hong_2007_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-Catherine_Hong_2007-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GwynethPaltrowByRichardYaussi2010.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1731" data-file-width="1384" height="275" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/GwynethPaltrowByRichardYaussi2010.jpg/220px-GwynethPaltrowByRichardYaussi2010.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/GwynethPaltrowByRichardYaussi2010.jpg/330px-GwynethPaltrowByRichardYaussi2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/GwynethPaltrowByRichardYaussi2010.jpg/440px-GwynethPaltrowByRichardYaussi2010.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GwynethPaltrowByRichardYaussi2010.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Paltrow at a ceremony for receiving her <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame" title="Hollywood Walk of Fame">Hollywood Walk of Fame</a> star, December 2010</div>
</div>
</div>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>Robert called me and he said, "This is gonna be fun, and this is gonna be good." And then he said to me, "Don't you want to be in a movie that people see?" And I was like, "Whoa! What would that feel like?" And he's right. Moviemaking is not supposed to be a masturbatory exercise; it's supposed to be shared by other people.</p>
</blockquote>
<p>In 2010, Paltrow reprised her role in the sequel to <i>Iron Man,</i> <i><a href="/wiki/Iron_Man_2" title="Iron Man 2">Iron Man 2</a>.</i> Later in 2010, she appeared in the musical <i><a href="/wiki/Country_Strong" title="Country Strong">Country Strong</a></i> and recorded the song <i>Country Strong</i> for the film's soundtrack.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> The song was released to country radio in August 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/83rd_Academy_Awards" title="83rd Academy Awards">83rd Academy Awards</a>, Paltrow performed another song from the movie, "<a href="/wiki/Country_Strong_(soundtrack)" title="Country Strong (soundtrack)">Coming Home</a>," which was nominated for Best Original Song.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>Paltrow also appeared in Fox's <i><a href="/wiki/Glee_(TV_series)" title="Glee (TV series)">Glee</a></i>, as substitute teacher <a href="/wiki/Holly_Holliday" title="Holly Holliday">Holly Holliday</a>, who fills in for <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Morrison" title="Matthew Morrison">Matthew Morrison</a>'s character when he falls ill. In her first episode, "The Substitute," she sang "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nowadays" title="Nowadays">Nowadays</a>" from the musical <a href="/wiki/Chicago_(musical)" title="Chicago (musical)"><i>Chicago</i></a> with <a href="/wiki/Lea_Michele" title="Lea Michele">Lea Michele</a>, <a href="/wiki/CeeLo_Green" title="CeeLo Green">CeeLo Green</a>'s "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fuck_You_(Cee_Lo_Green_song)" title="Fuck You (Cee Lo Green song)">Forget You</a>", and a mash-up of "<a href="/wiki/Singin%27_in_the_Rain_(song)" title="Singin' in the Rain (song)">Singin' In the Rain</a>" and <a href="/wiki/Rihanna" title="Rihanna">Rihanna</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Umbrella_(song)" title="Umbrella (song)">Umbrella</a>" with Morrison and the rest of the cast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>She later performed "Forget You" with CeeLo Green himself and several puppet characters provided by <a href="/wiki/The_Jim_Henson_Company" title="The Jim Henson Company">The Jim Henson Company</a> at the <a href="/wiki/53rd_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="53rd Annual Grammy Awards">2011 Grammy Awards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> She reprised her role twice more that season, performing <a href="/wiki/Do_You_Wanna_Touch_Me" title="Do You Wanna Touch Me">"Do You Wanna Touch Me (Oh Yeah)</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Gary_Glitter" title="Gary Glitter">Gary Glitter</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Acoustic_music" title="Acoustic music">acoustic</a> version of "<a href="/wiki/Landslide_(Fleetwood_Mac_song)" title="Landslide (Fleetwood Mac song)">Landslide</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Fleetwood_Mac" title="Fleetwood Mac">Fleetwood Mac</a>, "<a href="/wiki/Kiss_(Prince_song)" title="Kiss (Prince song)">Kiss</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Prince_(musician)" title="Prince (musician)">Prince</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Adele" title="Adele">Adele</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Turning_Tables" title="Turning Tables">Turning Tables</a>".</p>
<p>In 2011, Paltrow appeared in the <a href="/wiki/Steven_Soderbergh" title="Steven Soderbergh">Steven Soderbergh</a> thriller <i><a href="/wiki/Contagion_(film)" title="Contagion (film)">Contagion</a></i>, in which she was part of an ensemble cast, including <a href="/wiki/Kate_Winslet" title="Kate Winslet">Kate Winslet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marion_Cotillard" title="Marion Cotillard">Marion Cotillard</a> and her <i>The Talented Mr. Ripley</i> co-stars Matt Damon and Jude Law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> The movie opened at number 1 at the US Box Office Weekend and received positive reviews. In 2012 she starred in the independent romantic comedy <i><a href="/wiki/Thanks_for_Sharing" title="Thanks for Sharing">Thanks for Sharing</a></i> with <a href="/wiki/Mark_Ruffalo" title="Mark Ruffalo">Mark Ruffalo</a> and reprised her role as <a href="/wiki/Pepper_Potts" title="Pepper Potts">Pepper Potts</a> in the film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Avengers_(2012_film)" title="The Avengers (2012 film)">The Avengers</a></i>, which broke records as the highest grossing U.S. opening weekend film of all time. It was confirmed that Paltrow will star as <a href="/wiki/Dora_Maar" title="Dora Maar">Dora Maar</a> in <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Saura" title="Carlos Saura">Carlos Saura</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Spain" title="Cinema of Spain">Spanish film</a> <i>33 días</i> alongside <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Banderas" title="Antonio Banderas">Antonio Banderas</a> as <a href="/wiki/Pablo_Picasso" title="Pablo Picasso">Pablo Picasso</a>. The film began shooting in late 2012, for a 2013 release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>In April 2013, Paltrow was named <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People_(American_magazine)" title="People (American magazine)">People</a></i> magazine's annual "Most Beautiful Woman".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> In 2015, she co-starred in the film <i><a href="/wiki/Mortdecai_(film)" title="Mortdecai (film)">Mortdecai</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mortdecai_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mortdecai-56">[56]</a></sup> alongside <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Depp" title="Johnny Depp">Johnny Depp</a>, <a href="/wiki/Olivia_Munn" title="Olivia Munn">Olivia Munn</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Paul_Bettany" title="Paul Bettany">Paul Bettany</a>. Paltrow was also featured on the track "<a href="/wiki/Everglow" title="Everglow">Everglow</a>", which was included in <a href="/wiki/Coldplay" title="Coldplay">Coldplay</a>'s seventh studio album <i><a href="/wiki/A_Head_Full_of_Dreams" title="A Head Full of Dreams">A Head Full of Dreams</a></i> (2015).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_projects">Other projects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwyneth_Paltrow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Other projects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gwyneth_Paltrow_2012.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2761" data-file-width="2052" height="296" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Gwyneth_Paltrow_2012.jpg/220px-Gwyneth_Paltrow_2012.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Gwyneth_Paltrow_2012.jpg/330px-Gwyneth_Paltrow_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Gwyneth_Paltrow_2012.jpg/440px-Gwyneth_Paltrow_2012.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gwyneth_Paltrow_2012.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Paltrow at the <a href="/wiki/84th_Academy_Awards" title="84th Academy Awards">84th Academy Awards</a> in 2012</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Paltrow is a <a href="/wiki/Save_the_Children" title="Save the Children">Save the Children</a> artist ambassador, raising awareness about <a href="/wiki/World_Pneumonia_Day" title="World Pneumonia Day">World Pneumonia Day</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> She is on the board of the <a href="/wiki/Robin_Hood_Foundation" title="Robin Hood Foundation">Robin Hood Foundation</a>, a charitable organization that works to alleviate poverty in New York City.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> In February 2009, Paltrow received a Grammy nomination for her reading of the classic bear books of author <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bill_Martin,_Jr." title="Bill Martin, Jr.">Bill Martin, Jr.</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>Paltrow had her singing debut in the 2000 film <i><a href="/wiki/Duets_(film)" title="Duets (film)">Duets</a></i>, in which she performed a <a href="/wiki/Cover_version" title="Cover version">cover version</a> of <a href="/wiki/Smokey_Robinson" title="Smokey Robinson">Smokey Robinson</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Cruisin%27_(Smokey_Robinson_song)" title="Cruisin' (Smokey Robinson song)">Cruisin'</a>". The song was released as a single. The song went to number one in Australia, while Paltrow's rendition of the <a href="/wiki/Kim_Carnes" title="Kim Carnes">Kim Carnes</a> classic "<a href="/wiki/Bette_Davis_Eyes" title="Bette Davis Eyes">Bette Davis Eyes</a>" reached number three.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the 2006 film <i><a href="/wiki/Infamous_(film)" title="Infamous (film)">Infamous</a></i>, she sang "What Is This Thing Called Love". On September 27, 2006, Paltrow sang with <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">rapper</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a> during his concert at <a href="/wiki/Royal_Albert_Hall" title="Royal Albert Hall">Royal Albert Hall</a>. She sang the chorus for "<a href="/wiki/Song_Cry" title="Song Cry">Song Cry</a>", from the rapper's album <i><a href="/wiki/The_Blueprint" title="The Blueprint">Blueprint</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> In an interview, she said she would be at the concert but not that she would perform. She was quoted as saying "I'm a Jay-Z fan. He's my best friend."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2005, Paltrow became the face of <a href="/wiki/Est%C3%A9e_Lauder_Companies" title="Estée Lauder Companies">Estée Lauder's</a> Pleasures perfume. She appeared in Chicago on August 17, 2007, to sign bottles of the perfume, and on July 8, 2008, she promoted Lauder's Sensuous perfume in New York with the company's three other models.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> Estée Lauder donates a minimum of $500,000 of sales of items from the 'Pleasures Gwyneth Paltrow' collection to breast cancer research.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> In 2006, she became the face for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bean_Pole_International" title="Bean Pole International">Bean Pole International</a>, a Korean fashion brand.</p>
<p>In April 2009, Paltrow narrated <i>Brown Bear &amp; Friends</i>, the first of several children's audiobooks that she would narrate by Bill Martin. The <i>Brown Bear &amp; Friends</i> audiobook received a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Spoken_Word_Album_for_Children" title="Grammy Award for Best Spoken Word Album for Children">Grammy nomination</a> in 2009 for Best Spoken Word Album for Children. Since, she has also narrated Bill Martin's <i>Brown Bear, Brown Bear, What Do You See?</i>, <i>Baby Bear, Baby Bear, What Do You See?</i>, <i>Panda Bear, Panda Bear, What Do You See?</i>, and <i>Polar Bear, Polar Bear, What Do You Hear?</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2014, Paltrow partnered with Blo Blow Bar, teaming up with the brand's creative branch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>In October 2014, she hosted a <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic</a> fundraiser attended by President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> at her private residence in Los Angeles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2015, Paltrow announced plans to build a private club called The Arts Club at the former Hustler Store location <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Food_writing_and_Goop">Food writing and <i>Goop</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwyneth_Paltrow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Food writing and Goop">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In October 2007, Paltrow signed for the <a href="/wiki/PBS" title="PBS">PBS</a> television series <i><a href="/wiki/Spain..._on_the_Road_Again" title="Spain... on the Road Again">Spain... on the Road Again</a></i>, which showcases <a href="/wiki/Spanish_cuisine" title="Spanish cuisine">the food</a> and <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Spain" title="Culture of Spain">culture of Spain</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2008, she launched the weekly lifestyle newsletter <i>Goop</i>, encouraging readers to 'nourish the inner aspect'. The website's title is derived from her initials.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> The website includes a store, including among its wares a vaginal jade egg which some gynecologists say is unsafe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2008, she co-wrote the book <i>Spain... A Culinary Road Trip</i> with <a href="/wiki/Mario_Batali" title="Mario Batali">Mario Batali</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> In 2011, she wrote a book titled <i>My Father's Daughter: Delicious, Easy Recipes Celebrating Family and Togetherness</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> That same year she penned the book <i>Notes From the Kitchen Table</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> Two years later she published a book titled <i>It's All Good: Delicious Easy Recipes That Will Make You Look Good and Feel Great</i>. That year she wrote a foreword for a book by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ross_Matthews" title="Ross Matthews">Ross Matthews</a>, <i>Man Up! Tales of My Delusional Self-Confidence</i>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwyneth_Paltrow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>At the age of 24, Paltrow was engaged to actor <a href="/wiki/Brad_Pitt" title="Brad Pitt">Brad Pitt</a>, whom she dated from 1994 to 1997.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> The engagement was called off, according to Paltrow, because she was not ready for marriage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> Paltrow has since said that, as this was her first high-profile relationship with another celebrity, it taught her the need for public discretion about her romantic life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gwyneth_Paltrow_avp_Iron_Man_3_Paris_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="748" data-file-width="526" height="242" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Gwyneth_Paltrow_avp_Iron_Man_3_Paris_2.jpg/170px-Gwyneth_Paltrow_avp_Iron_Man_3_Paris_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Gwyneth_Paltrow_avp_Iron_Man_3_Paris_2.jpg/255px-Gwyneth_Paltrow_avp_Iron_Man_3_Paris_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Gwyneth_Paltrow_avp_Iron_Man_3_Paris_2.jpg/340px-Gwyneth_Paltrow_avp_Iron_Man_3_Paris_2.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gwyneth_Paltrow_avp_Iron_Man_3_Paris_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Paltrow at the <i><a href="/wiki/Iron_Man_3" title="Iron Man 3">Iron Man 3</a></i> French premiere in April 2013</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Paltrow had an on-off three-year relationship with actor <a href="/wiki/Ben_Affleck" title="Ben Affleck">Ben Affleck</a> from 1997 to late 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Affleck_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-Affleck-80">[80]</a></sup> They first broke up in early 1999 but, soon after their breakup, Paltrow persuaded Affleck to star in the film <i><a href="/wiki/Bounce_(film)" title="Bounce (film)">Bounce</a></i> with her;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> during the making of the film, which was shot in mid-1999, the couple started dating again and eventually broke up in October 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Affleck_80-1"><a href="#cite_note-Affleck-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<p>In October 2002, Paltrow met <a href="/wiki/Chris_Martin" title="Chris Martin">Chris Martin</a> of the British rock group <a href="/wiki/Coldplay" title="Coldplay">Coldplay</a> backstage three weeks after the death of her father, <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Paltrow" title="Bruce Paltrow">Bruce Paltrow</a>. They married on December 5, 2003, in a ceremony at a hotel in <a href="/wiki/Southern_California" title="Southern California">Southern California</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HiscockTele_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-HiscockTele-82">[82]</a></sup> Paltrow and Martin have two children together: daughter Apple Blythe Alison Martin (b. 2004) and son Moses Bruce Anthony Martin (b. 2006).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boy_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-boy-83">[83]</a></sup> Paltrow explained Apple's unusual first name on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Oprah_Winfrey_Show" title="The Oprah Winfrey Show">Oprah</a></i>, saying: "It sounded so sweet and it conjured such a lovely picture for me – you know, apples are so sweet and they're wholesome and it's biblical – and I just thought it sounded so lovely and ... clean! And I just thought, 'Perfect!'."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> She explained her son's first name came from the song, "<a href="/wiki/Moses_(song)" title="Moses (song)">Moses</a>", that her husband wrote for her before their <a href="/wiki/Wedding" title="Wedding">wedding</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boy_83-1"><a href="#cite_note-boy-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2014 Paltrow, who was raised in a Jewish and Christian household, said she was converting to Judaism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dailymail_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dailymail-85">[85]</a></sup> She had earlier discovered that her father came from a long line of influential Eastern European rabbis, which inspired her to raise her daughter and son in a Jewish environment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dailymail_85-1"><a href="#cite_note-Dailymail-85">[85]</a></sup> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> She joked that she was a "Jewish princess" after learning there were 17 generations of rabbis in her family tree.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dailymail_85-2"><a href="#cite_note-Dailymail-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>Paltrow cut down on work after becoming a mother.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> She also suffered from <a href="/wiki/Postpartum_depression" title="Postpartum depression">postpartum depression</a> after the 2006 birth of her son.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-depression_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-depression-88">[88]</a></sup> In March 2014, Paltrow announced that she and Martin had separated after ten years of marriage, describing the process as "conscious uncoupling".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-people.com_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-people.com-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> In April 2015, Paltrow filed for divorce from Chris Martin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> A judge finalized their divorce on July 15, 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2013, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> reported Paltrow to be a practitioner of <a href="/wiki/Transcendental_Meditation_technique" title="Transcendental Meditation technique">Transcendental Meditation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYTfeb13_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYTfeb13-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>In August 2014, Paltrow started dating <i><a href="/wiki/Glee_(TV_series)" title="Glee (TV series)">Glee</a></i> co-creator <a href="/wiki/Brad_Falchuk" title="Brad Falchuk">Brad Falchuk</a>, whom she met whilst filming the series in 2010, 2011, and 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usmagazine.com_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-usmagazine.com-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2000, Dante Soiu was charged after allegedly sending Paltrow sex toys and hundreds of unsolicited letters, many of a sexual nature;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McCartney_.282016-02-10.29_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-McCartney_.282016-02-10.29-94">[94]</a></sup> he pleaded not guilty by reason of insanity and was confined to a mental institution for several years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McCartney_.282016-02-17.29_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-McCartney_.282016-02-17.29-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Telegraph_.282016.29_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraph_.282016.29-96">[96]</a></sup> Soiu was again arrested in 2015 after sending Paltrow dozens of packages and letters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Telegraph_.282016.29_96-1"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraph_.282016.29-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McCartney_.282016-02-17.29_95-1"><a href="#cite_note-McCartney_.282016-02-17.29-95">[95]</a></sup> His trial took place in February 2016 and he was acquitted of the charges on February 17, 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McCartney_.282016-02-17.29_95-2"><a href="#cite_note-McCartney_.282016-02-17.29-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Filmography">Filmography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwyneth_Paltrow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Filmography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
